                                              Various Degrees of Glory
       Like a variety of other interpreters, whom we have surveyed in the present book, Connell correctly affirms
that 1Cor 15:41-42 is referring to various degrees of misthological glory:

      Some Believers Shine like the Sun…Others will not (Resurrection Glory)
      * Some believers will shine like the sun, others like the moon, and others like a faint star
      (1 Cor. 15:41-42).
      * There are many billions of stars, and each is unique.
      * The Pistol Star is 10 million times brighter than our sun and has a mass 100 times greater.
      * In the age to come, there might be several billion people in God’s family.
      * The realm of “the resurrection” includes our body, garment, thrones, crowns, and more—each area
      of our life in the resurrection will express a measure of the glory of God.
      * The degree of glory that we will have is based upon the way we live on earth.
      * The degree of glory in our resurrected bodies will be directly related to what we overcome in this
      life and the amount of Christ-likeness that has been formed within us.
      No two believers will have the same measure of glory. (P. 68)
                                               Partial Resurrection
       His assertion of varying degrees of glory is common, as we have seen. What is uncommon is that Connell
limits the resurrection before the millennial kingdom to faithful believers. Yet this proposition is consistent with
the millennial-kingdom-exclusionist position that he has taken:

              The first resurrection, I believe, is a resurrection of reward. I believe that participation in the
      first resurrection is reserved for those who are overcomers. It would be helpful for you to understand
      that there is a significant point of difference of doctrine about this issue, and not everyone will be
      happy if you take this position; but I believe it’s a true position....some Christians…believe that all
      believers will be in the first resurrection. That’s a position, and there’s some scriptural support for that;
      but others believe that the first resurrection is a prize, and therefore not automatic. That’s the position
      I’ve taken, for many, many years: that the First Resurrection is a Resurrection of Reward - a prize to
      be won. (P. 126).

             Here is the controversial part...Although only believers are in the First Resurrection, there’s
      nothing anywhere says that all believers will be in that resurrection. In fact, there’s several descriptions
      which indicate quite the opposite - that it’s limited. It says: those who participate in the First
      Resurrection will rule and reign with Christ in the millennium - that’s very clear!
             That promise is given to overcomers, in Revelations 2 & 3. The promise of ruling is part of the
      First Resurrection; and the promise given to overcomers is ruling with Christ; so quite clearly,
      overcomers are the people that have qualified to enter into this First Resurrection, and participate in
      ruling and reign with Him, and establishing His kingdom on earth.
             Clearly, not all Christians are overcomers - many are overcome….
             ….There are many, many people; and there are both believers and unbelievers in the Second
      Resurrection. The only people that won’t be in the Second Resurrection will be the overcomers,
      because they come up in the first one. The Second Resurrection - that’s those who are alive at that
      time, who are changed; and those who have died, will be raised at that time. Now whether they’re
      believers or unbelievers, they will all appear before Christ, and there will be a judgement. This one is
      called the Great White Throne Judgement, in comparison to the other one we looked at, which is just
      the Bema, the Judgement (or rewards) Seat of Christ. Believers and unbelievers are both in the Second
      Resurrection. We know that, because people are found written in the Book of Life, so that means
      they’re a believer. The First Resurrection contains believers; but not all believers, only overcomers.
      (Pp. 328-330)

        He also argues that the out-resurrection in Phil 3:11 is a reward limited to faithful believers who overcome,
as is the better resurrection in Heb 11:35. He is correct on both accounts. The out-resurrection is a reward, as is the
better resurrection. However, the explanation posed in TOD for such texts as these, along with Rev 20:6 and
Appendix 3. Unglorified Believers                                                                                Page 83
Lk 20:35, remains superior in that certain texts (such as Dan 12:2; 1Thess 4:16-17; 1Cor 15:22-23; 51-52) indicate
that the resurrection of all believers, both faithful and unfaithful, is simultaneous for their respective time periods
(the rapture for church-age believers and the end of the tribulation for tribulational believers). Unfaithful and faithful
believers of each respective timeframe are summoned to stand before their respective Bema judgments before the
millennial kingdom commences.
       Contrariwise to such misthologists as Connell, my argument in ch. 3 of TOD is that what is at stake for
believers is a special status in the first resurrection, not basic participation in the resurrection. Having a portion in
that resurrection means more than having basic participation in it. Likewise, being worthy of that resurrection means
more than merely experiencing that resurrection. Only overcomers will attain this special status in the first
resurrection. At any rate, like myself, Connell believes that the Heavenly City is a reward limited to faithful
believers and that unfaithful believers are cast into the outer darkness. He apparently places the outer darkness on
Earth and thinks that unfaithful believers will serve there in lowly priestly capacities in unglorified bodies as
opposed to resurrected believers who will serve from the Heavenly City as resurrected glorified rulers. He uses
typology regarding the priesthood to make his point:

      No picture in the Bible is perfect, but you'll see the transition.…Levi, and the priesthood of Levi, was
      replaced by Melchizedek, or by Zadok. 1 Samuel 2:35 – “I will raise up for Myself a faithful priest,
      who shall do according to what’s in My heart and My mind. I will build him a sure house; he will walk
      before My anointed forever.” Eli was replaced by Eleazar. He was replaced by Abiatha; and then when
      it came to King Solomon, and the coming millennial rule, He replaced the priesthood, put another one
      in. So, the millennial rule has a different priesthood. So why did He put Zadok in there; and why is it
      that Levi forfeited there? It all goes back to a man called Eli, and he’s found in the first Book of
      Samuel, in the first few chapters. Eli was the high priest, and God was planning a massive change, so
      He raised up Samuel, who became the prophet and priest to the nation.
             This is in 1 Samuel 2:29-30, and I encourage you to read this story yourself. Eli was old, and
      blind - had no vision. Eli was very heavy, a big fat man; and what happened was that his sons, who
      were also the priests, were stealing the best offerings for themselves; and they were also being involved
      in sexual immorality with the women who came to worship. God spoke to Eli, and said this: Why do
      you kick at My sacrifice, and My offering, which I have commanded in My dwelling? You honour
      your sons more than Me, to make yourselves fat with the best of the offerings! Then He said: “therefore
      the Lord God of Israel says: I said indeed your house and the house of your father would walk with
      Me forever.”
             In other words, this was going to be a forever job - but now it’s far from Me. Those who honour
      Me, I will honour; but those who despise Me, shall be lightly esteemed. He then lays out exactly what's
      going to happen. He puts a curse on them. He says: in your family no one will ever get old, they'll all
      die prematurely; and He said: here’s a sign for you. On one day, both of your sons will die. So on one
      day, both of his sons died in battle; and when the news came back to Eli, it was such a shock for him
      that the sons had died, and the ark had been captured, that he fell over and broke his neck. There’s
      symbolism in all of these things, but the key thing in here was: there was a lack of relationship with
      God.
             Here’s the reasons they forfeited the priesthood. The bottom line is: they dishonoured God;
      and they honoured themselves - that was why they forfeited their priesthood. In any priesthood,
      which includes us, in any leadership, any kind of ministry… if we dishonour God in our actions, and
      honour yourself - you will forfeit your priesthood in eternity! Very, very serious! It’s a huge issue!
             God called it: “they dishonoured Me”. He said to Eli: “you honour your sons more than Me.
      You make yourselves fat with all the best of the offerings”. So read the story, there were three things
      that were identified: 1) Lack of intimate relationship with the Lord. It says: “they were sons of Belial,
      they did not know the Lord”. Now that seems crazy! Here they are, they’re serving in the tabernacle,
      all the things of God. They’re fully involved in the religious system, yet there’s no intimacy or
      relationship with the Lord. It’s a very strong picture of people who have no ongoing personal
      relationship with the Lord - they're just fulfilling religious roles, religious duties. No relationship with
      the Lord, and as a result, they have no respect or honour for Him. No respect, no honour. (Pp. 159-
      160)
Redeemed Bodies Versus Glorified Bodies                                                                        Page 84
I concur. Unfaithful believers forfeit their priesthood for all eternity. The conclusion, then, from this part of his
analysis, should be that unfaithful believers forfeit their priesthood in its entirety throughout the millennial kingdom
and throughout all eternity. Connell’s acknowledgment of the eternal forfeiture is consistent with the eternal nature
of the rewards and the loss thereof. Unfortunately, Connell tones down this conclusion to picture unfaithful believers
as serving in lowly priestly capacities in unglorified bodies on Earth during the millennial kingdom:

              The Bible uses the story of Eli and Zadok as a prophetic picture of the priesthood in the
      millennial age. You find Zadok mentioned in a couple of places. We find him mentioned 1 Kings 2:35;
      when Solomon became the king, he put then Zadok as priest in the place of Abiathar - that’s when
      Zadok came in.
              I encourage you to read around there. There was a lot of skulduggery going on, but Zadok
      remained faithful to God’s appointed king. In the story of Eli’s sons, they dishonoured God, as their
      king. They dishonoured God in their offerings, in their morality, their life, their attitudes, everything;
      but Zadok, he honoured God, and honoured God’s selection. The Bible talks about the transition, and
      it starts to then talk about the millennial impact of this, and so when we go into Ezekiel 44, I want you
      to see the prophetic picture in here as well. In the Old Testament, they had a natural temple, and natural
      sacrifices, so when he’s describing what he sees, he’s describing it through the natural. You’ve really
      got to see beyond that, to the supernatural.
              Ezekiel 44:10 – “The Levites who went far from Me, when Israel went astray, and who strayed
      from Me after their idols, shall bear their iniquity. Yet in spite of this…(and He’s saying there’s
      consequences for holding idols in your heart)…they shall be ministers in My sanctuary, as gatekeepers
      of the house and ministers of the house; they shall slay the burnt offering and sacrifice for the people,
      they’ll stand before them to minister to them. Because they ministered to them before their idols, and
      caused the house of Israel to fall into iniquity, I have raised My hand against them, said the Lord, and
      they shall bear their iniquity.
              Ezekiel 44:43 – “They will not come near to Me, to minister to Me as a priest. They’ll not come
      near to My holy things, they’ll not come near to the Most Holy Place. They will carry the shame of
      their conduct. Nevertheless, they will still work in the temple[.]”
              What is He saying then, with the sons of Levi? He’s saying then, in the coming millennium
      kingdom, this is what’ll happen...They will not receive a glorified resurrected body that can go
      backwards and forwards between heaven and earth - that’s the body Jesus had. The cost to any believer,
      of dishonouring God, and not being faithful in their priesthood to Him, is they will not receive that
      glorified, resurrected body. They will not be able to pass back and forth between heaven and earth,
      just as Jesus was able to do. They will not have access into the throne of God. They will not reign with
      Him on earth, and they will have a limited role serving in the earthly realm. They will have a role
      serving in the church, but they will not have the realm of being able to move and enter into the very
      throne room of God, and bring the supernatural life and power of God in a massive way back into the
      earth. They represent believers who are legalistic; there’s no transformation, they dishonour God. They
      dishonour God; and they’ve refused heart transformation. I see a lot of people like that - legalistic
      people, dishonouring to God in the way they conduct themselves, and not letting God into their heart
      to bring about transformation. It says: they will not come near to Me, to minister to Me as a priest.
      They will not come near any of My holy things. They will not enter the Holy Place. (Pp. 161-163)

       Apparently, if Connell is consistent with his earlier stance that “whatever He decides, regarding you, is
irreversible, and unchangeable,” then the extrapolation of his argument would lead to the conclusion that at the
end of the millennial age, unfaithful believers will receive a resurrected body but “will not receive a glorified
resurrected body.” The resurrected body they receive will be unglorified. The primary difference, in that case,
between his model and mine, is I pose that unfaithful believers who died before the beginning of the millennial
kingdom will be resurrected in unglorified immortal bodies and sent back to the outer realm celestial realm of the
universal kingdom as a result of the Bema. See Illustration 31. Celestial versus Terrestrial Outer Darkness (p. 80).
Unfaithful immortals will be excluded from the millennial kingdom, per se, in that the millennial kingdom is
normally associated with the terrestrial kingdom, ancestral kingdom, and misthopological kingdom. When the
millennial kingdom is narrowly defined in these terms, then my model poses a millennial exclusion for resurrected
unfaithful believers. On the other hand, unfaithful believers who live through the tribulation would be allowed to
Appendix 3. Unglorified Believers                                                                                  Page 85
enter the terrestrial kingdom in mortal bodies but excluded from the ancestral kingdom and misthopological
kingdom. Unfaithful mortals will live in the terrestrial kingdom but be excluded from the other two spatial aspects
of the kingdom associated with Earth. In that sense, they are also excluded from the millennial kingdom. My
modified model thus poses a limited millennial kingdom exclusion for both groups of unfaithful believers,
regardless as to whether they are immortal or mortal. But the nature of that exclusion varies according to their
mortal/immortal status.
        In contrast to Connell, however, I do not believe that unfaithful believers will be allowed to serve in the
earthly temple, even in unglorified bodies. TOD posed a better option, which I will abbreviate here with appropriate
tweaks. Those faithful earthly priests who survive the tribulation and thus are in mortal bodies and yet
genealogically represent those guilty of apostasy will bear the punishment of serving in a state of shame, but they
still will be within the complex (Eze 44:9-14); although, they will not be privy to the more intimate access granted
as a reward to those mortal priests who genealogically represent the faithful (Eze 44:15-16). Yet these faithful
priests must change clothing when passing back and forth between the inner and outer court (Eze 44:17-19) so that
holiness may not be transmitted to the Outer Court. The subsequent line of mortal Levitical priests will not be able
to minister in the sanctuary in the Millennium Temple because their forefathers did not remain faithful to the Lord.
Unfaithful OT Levitical priests will not be raised from the dead or physically allowed to minister, even in these
lowly positions, within the millennial temple (Eze 44:10-13). Instead, their descendants who enter the millennial
kingdom in mortal flesh and blood bodies will be allowed to serve in the temple and typologically represent the
unfaithful OT Levitical priests (who are raised from the dead but banished to the celestial outer darkness). Unfaithful
mortal believers are not allowed into the Promised Land. Rather, new Jewish believers and Jewish children below
the age of accountability who live until the end of the tribulation will be considered misthologically neutral and
enter the millennial kingdom (while living in mortal flesh and blood bodies) and will take care of the flesh and
blood animals within the restricted regions of the Promised Land and earthly Mount Zion.
        Connell seems to portray unresurrected unfaithful believers as serving in unglorified unresurrected bodies on
Earth as their outer darkness during the millennial kingdom. But if they are unresurrected, how are they able to
serve on Earth? Are they serving in ethereal bodies on Earth during the millennial kingdom? Per his comments,
why are they able to serve as lowly priests during the millennial kingdom before they are resurrected but unable to
serve as priests in the eternal state after they are resurrected? His discussion leaves such questions unanswered. My
perception is that Connell limits his millennial kingdom exclusion to the misthopological kingdom, whereas, in my
newer model being proposed herein, I would expand millennial kingdom exclusion to include the ancestral and
terrestrial kingdoms for unfaithful unglorified believers. In TOD, I posed that unfaithful resurrected believers were
excluded from the misthopological kingdom and ancestral kingdom. In my newer model, I have expanded that
exclusion to include the terrestrial kingdom for unfaithful immortals.
        If Connell is consistent with his millennial exclusion, then he should place unfaithful resurrected believers in
lowly positions of service in unglorified resurrected bodies in the ancestral and terrestrial kingdoms during the
eternal state. On the other hand, if he is consistent with his eternal exclusion from the priesthood, he should deny
unresurrected unfaithful believers any priestly service during the millennium. Some apparent inconsistencies and
logistical issues need to be worked out in his model. My model is comparatively simple. I pose that unfaithful
believers are resurrected and sent to the outer realm of the celestial kingdom, not to the ancestral or terrestrial realms
of the earthly kingdom. They are denied any positions of regal or priestly service. Unfaithful believers who live
until the end of the tribulation are sent to the terrestrial outer darkness to live out the remainder of their mortal lives.
At the end of the millennium, they are resurrected in the second resurrection, judged to be unfaithful, and sent in
their unglorified immortal bodies to live in the celestial outer darkness.
        Connell’s conclusion regarding Levi is acceptable if it is limited to the physical descendants of Levi below
the age of accountability who survive the tribulation. In that case, it is much like my position. His position can be
read with full appreciation when seen from that perspective:

       - The Sons of Levi
       - In the Millennial Kingdom they will not receive a glorified resurrected body that can go back and
       forth between heaven and earth such as the body Jesus had following His resurrection
       - They will not have access into the realm of heaven and the throne of God, nor reign with Him on
       earth
       - They will be limited to ministering in the earthly realm, they will have a role serving the house (P.
       177).
Redeemed Bodies Versus Glorified Bodies                                                                           Page 86
                                               Kingdom Entrance
      According to Connell, when Jesus says that He does not know those performing miracles in His name, and
then denies them entrance into the kingdom of heaven in Mt 7:21-27, He is denying that they know Him intimately,
so Jesus bars them from entering the millennial kingdom: “In this passage, Jesus is referring to entrance to the
coming millennial kingdom, and the accompanying rewards. The thing at stake here is the entrance to coming
kingdom” (p. 279). “Our entrance into heaven is not based on our works, though our status and our role in
the Kingdom of Heaven is” (p. 282).

      He cast this unprofitable servant out into the outer darkness, where there be weeping and gnashing of
      teeth. He becomes excluded from the Marriage Supper and celebration. There was no benefit in all I
      invested in Him, no tangible benefit to the kingdom. “He will be cast into the outer darkness, where
      there be weeping and gnashing of teeth”. What is the ‘outer darkness’; and what is the ‘weeping and
      gnashing of teeth’? Some Christians think the ‘outer darkness’ refers to hell, and this is a story about
      whether they're saved or unsaved, but that cannot be true, and here are two reasons why it can’t be
      true… 1) Firstly, it calls it ‘outer darkness’, but hell is described as a place of ‘burning’ - so it can't be
      burning, and dark, at the same time - it doesn’t make sense! 2) Secondly, our works do not qualify us
      for heaven; faith in the work of Christ does. He’s talking here about reward versus loss….
        ….So ‘outer darkness’ refers to the conditions outside the banquet hall, meaning exclusion from the
      celebration of the marriage feast. (Pp. 305-306)

       Since Connell poses that those in the outer darkness are in Heaven, not burning in Hell, this aspect of his
model appears very close to my celestial outer darkness. Also, he apparently concurs that we enter the kingdom of
God at the point of the new birth: “With every child that’s born in the kingdom of God, God takes you into a
process of growth, with a purpose of changing you” (p. 363). Some misthologists pose that the kingdom of God is
a more comprehensive term than the kingdom of heaven and take the former term soteriologically and the latter
misthologically. I do not. Instead, I am using the term universal kingdom (with a restricted understanding) to
designate this soteriological dimension. Terminology aside, Connell and I appear to be making similar claims. All
believers are spatially in the kingdom in one sense of the word, but not in another sense of the word. Also, regarding
2Pet 1:11, Connell would likewise juxtapose an abundant entrance into the kingdom against a meager entrance:
“We can have an abundant entrance to the kingdom, or we can barely scrape in. I think it’s better to have an
abundance” (p. 370). True, all believers enter the kingdom soteriologically, but only faithful believers enter it
misthologically/magnificently. The primary difference between my model and that of Connell is that he poses a
partial resurrection and partial rapture.
                                                Partial Rapture
      In harmony with his partial resurrection position, Connell advocates a partial rapture:

            1 Thessalonians 4:13 – “When the trump of God sounds, the dead in Christ shall rise first”.
            In the Old Testament, when He sounded one trumpet, all those who were leaders would gather.
      So when the trump sounds, you notice the overcomers will arise, and they are the ones who will rule
      with Christ, so you see a strong picture prophetically in the Old Testament, of two different situations:
      one trumpet, the leaders or rulers arise; the other trumpet, the whole congregation arises. When the
      Lord returns, one trump will sound, and then the overcomers will arise into their resurrection bodies.
      It won’t be until the end of 1000 years that the two trumpets will sound, and all the rest are gathered.
      Imagine that! (Pp. 337-338).

Since I have refuted the partial rapture position elsewhere (see TOD and DFS), doing so here is unnecessary. Suffice
it to say that the Thessalonian context affirms the rapture of all believers and their deliverance from the wrath of
the Day of the Lord, regardless of their being morally awake or asleep, but conditions their misthological salvation
on their being morally awake (1Thess 5:9-10). Additionally, the unfaithful servants are cast into the outer darkness
at the same time the faithful servants are put in charge of cities and enter the wedding festivities. Therefore, the
corresponding rapture and/or resurrection and judgment of the unfaithful is not delayed until 1000 years later.
Connell’s own statement leads to this conclusion:
Appendix 3. Unglorified Believers                                                                                Page 87
              In the parables, the three servants all have to give account at the same time. The Bible tells
      us that the accounting for believers is all together, at the judgement seat of Christ. The accounting
      for the rest of the world, and unbelievers, is all at the end of the millennial reign; so, the fact they're
      all called to account together, points also to the fact they must be believers. (P. 401).

       Yes, these three servants are believers, but they must be raptured/resurrected all together at the same time to
stand before the same Bema. Consequently, the unfaithful servant must be raptured/raised and judged at the same
time as the two faithful servants. For church-age believers, this will be the Judgment Seat of Christ that occurs at
the end of the tribulation. Per Connell’s own statement, a partial rapture position is untenable. Therefore, a partial
resurrection of only some of the church-age believers at the time of the rapture is unreasonable. For the sake of
internal consistency, his discussion should be amended to acknowledge that unfaithful church-age believers are
resurrected but judged at the Bema as being unqualified to have glorified bodies.
                                                  Conclusion
      Although I have suggested serval improvements to Connell’s position, I am admonished, in light of the
present study, to adopt a tweak from him regarding my own position. He states:

      What is “Outer Darkness”?
      * Many Christians think that “outer darkness” refers to hell.
      * This is a mistake and brings confusion concerning the real possibility of a believer being excluded
      from ruling with Christ in His coming Kingdom
      * Outer darkness does not refer to hell. It is referring to a different state or condition (p. 421).

Until this study, I thought that all resurrected believers would be in a glorified state and thus have at least some
degree of glory, thinking that one might picture unfaithful resurrected believers as shining like fireflies in the
darkness in contrast to beaming like stars. As a result of this study, I now believe that unfaithful resurrected believers
will not even have that degree of glory. The current study supports the contention of misthologists such as Connell
who assert that unfaithful believers will not have glorified bodies. Redeemed bodies, yes. Glorified bodies, no.
Unfaithful believers will be in an unglorified state/condition throughout eternity. Connell’s book is a worthy
devotional read for a perspective similar to my own on the major points. Throughout eternity, the Bridal City is
limited to glorified believers, namely to those who are faithful. Unfaithful believers are left in unglorified bodies in
the outer darkness inside Heaven but outside the Heavenly City. On these principal points, we appear to agree.
